        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript.


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

        output: >-
          Genes collaborate with each other to perform their functions in
          specific contexts. To understand how these genes influence complex
          traits, a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across
          different conditions is essential for developing novel therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have identified the role of
          individual genes in disease mechanisms. However, modern models suggest
          that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
          progression.


          PhenoPLIER is a computational approach designed to map gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
          latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is based
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions, highlighting their importance in understanding diseases'
          etiology and drug mechanisms. We observe that diseases are
          significantly associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell
          types and find our approach to be accurate in predicting known
          drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action.


          Moreover, using a CRISPR screen for analyzing lipid regulation, we
          identify functionally important players lacking associations but
          prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In conclusion,
          integrating groups of co-expressed genes through the lens of gene
          modules provides context to genetic associations, enabling the
          discovery and validation of potential targets missed by single-gene
          strategies.


          PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic
          associations and exploring disease etiology, providing valuable
          insights into drug repurposing and mechanisms of action.

        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure and
          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.


          Revised paragraph:
        display: >-
          /home/miltondp/projects/others/manubot/manubot-ai-editor-evals/abstract/prompts/candidate.txt
      vars: *ref_1
      response:
        output: >-
          This manuscript aims to bridge the gap between genetic studies and
          functional genomics by utilizing gene co-expression patterns to
          elucidate disease etiology, drug mechanisms, and therapeutic targets.
          To achieve this, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel computational
          approach that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological
          perturbation data into a common latent representation for joint
          analysis. This method is based on modules of genes with similar
          expression patterns across the same conditions, thereby capturing
          gene-gene interactions in complex traits.


          We demonstrate the effectiveness of PhenoPLIER by accurately
          predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
          action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
          regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework for
          interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene modules,
          contextualizing these relationships and revealing potential targets
          missed by single-gene strategies. By integrating groups of
          co-expressed genes, this approach sheds light on complex traits and
          has broad implications in drug repurposing efforts.

        output: >-
          Genes perform their functions in concert with each other, requiring a
          mechanistic understanding of gene expression regulation across
          different contexts for predicting complex traits. Transcriptome-wide
          association studies have helped uncover the role of individual genes
          in disease mechanisms; however, modern models predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.

          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
          latent representation for joint analysis based on modules of
          co-expressed genes across the same conditions. Our study reveals
          significant association with gene modules expressed in relevant cell
          types, accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs, and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Additionally, we found that functionally
          important players are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation.


          In conclusion, incorporating groups of co-expressed genes with
          PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential
          targets missed by single-gene strategies. This novel framework for
          interpreting genetic associations through gene modules provides
          insights into disease etiology and drug mechanisms, enabling the
          repurposing of existing drugs to treat complex diseases.

          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concierto with each other in specifico
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is base on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantl
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          The genetic basis of complex traits and diseases remains elusive due
          to the intricate interplay between genes in specific contexts.
          Understanding gene regulation is critical for developing new
          therapies, yet transcriptome-wide association studies alone cannot
          fully capture this complexity. Modern models predict that gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.


          PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach, maps gene-trait
          associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
          latent representation for joint analysis. It identifies modules of
          co-expressed genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions, revealing significant associations between diseases and
          these modules. This study demonstrates PhenoPLIER's accuracy in
          predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
          action. Furthermore, using CRISPR screening to analyze lipid
          regulation, we find that functionally important players are
          prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER despite lacking
          associations.


          In conclusion, PhenoPLIER contextualizes genetic associations through
          the lens of gene modules, revealing potential targets missed by
          single-gene strategies. This approach provides a novel framework for
          interpreting genetic associations and drug mechanisms, thus advancing
          our understanding of complex traits and diseases.

          In this study, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel computational method
          that facilitates the mapping of gene-trait associations and
          pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent representation
          for joint analysis. We emphasize the collaborative nature of genes in
          performing their functions; to understand how these genes influence
          complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of expression
          regulation across different conditions. This insight is essential for
          developing new therapies, as transcriptome-wide association studies
          have uncovered the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
          mechanisms. However, modern models predict that gene-gene interactions
          play a critical role in disease origin and progression.


          PhenoPLIER's approach relies on modules of co-expressed genes with
          similar expression patterns across relevant cell types to associate
          diseases significantly with these functional units. Our method is
          accurate at predicting known drug-disease pairs, as well as inferring
          mechanisms of action. Further, using a CRISPR screen for lipid
          regulation analysis, we find that functionally important players in
          trait-associated modules lack associations but are prioritized by
          PhenoPLIER.


          In conclusion, incorporating groups of co-expressed genes helps
          contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets missed
          by single-gene strategies. By utilizing gene modules, PhenoPLIER
          offers a novel framework for interpreting complex traits and
          identifying therapeutic targets. This approach provides valuable
          insights into the disease etiology and drug mechanisms that could
          guide future research in functional genomics.

          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach
          that maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation
          data into a common latent representation for a joint analysis. Genes
          act in concert with each other in specific contexts to perform their
          functions. Determining how these genes influence complex traits
          requires a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across
          different conditions. It has been shown that this insight is critical
          for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies
          have helped uncover the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
          mechanisms. However, modern models of the architecture of complex
          traits predict that gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in
          disease origin and progression. PhenoPLIER's representation is based
          on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
          conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly associated with
          gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach is
          accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          We introduce PhenoPLIER, a cutting-edge computational approach that
          integrates gene expression data and pharmacological perturbation
          information into a common latent representation for joint analysis. By

          and uncover potential targets overlooked by traditional single-gene
          strategies. By providing a novel framework for interpreting gene
          module relationships, PhenoPLIER enhances our understanding of complex
          traits and their associated diseases.

          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations

        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure and
          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies. Our
          results in this study show that diseases are significantly associated
          with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
          is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          In the field of genetic studies and functional genomics, complex
          traits are often associated with clusters of co-expressed genes.
          However, understanding how these gene modules influence disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms remains an open question. To address this
          gap in the literature, our study introduces PhenoPLIER, a novel
          approach for projecting genetic associations through gene expression
          patterns. 


          Here, we demonstrate that diseases are significantly associated with
          specific cell types, as determined by gene modules expressed under

          drug-disease pairs and identifies mechanisms of action. Moreover,
          using CRISPR screening to analyze lipid regulation, we find that
          functionally important players lack associations but are prioritized
          in trait-associated modules.

          contextualizing complex traits and revealing potential drug targets
          missed by single-gene strategies. By incorporating groups of
          co-expressed genes, this approach enhances our understanding of
          disease etiology and therapeutic mechanisms, ultimately advancing drug
          repurposing efforts in the pharmaceutical industry.

        raw: >-
          You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
          improving the text of a manuscript with title 'Projecting genetic
          associations through gene expression patterns highlights disease
          etiology and drug mechanisms' and keywords 'genetic studies,
          functional genomics, gene co-expression, therapeutic targets, drug
          repurposing, clustering of complex traits.' Revise the following
          abstract of this manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure and
          follows a context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a
          single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary
          to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies. Our
          results in this study show that diseases are significantly associated
          with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our approach
          is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
          mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze
          lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
          associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, by incorporating groups of co-expressed
          genes, PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal
          potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
          provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
          through the lens of gene modules.

          Genes collaborate in unison to perform their functions under specific
          conditions, which necessitates a mechanistic understanding of gene
          expression across different contexts for complex trait determination.
          Recent studies have demonstrated that this insight is crucial for
          developing novel therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies
          (TWAS) have contributed significantly to uncovering the role of
          individual genes within disease-relevant mechanisms; however,
          contemporary models of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a pivotal part in disease origin and progression.


          In this study, we introduce PhenoPLIER - a computational approach
          designed for mapping gene-trait associations with pharmacological
          perturbation data into a common latent representation suitable for
          joint analysis. The underlying structure is based on modules
          comprising genes exhibiting similar expression patterns across the
          same conditions. We observe that diseases exhibit significant
          association with specific gene modules expressed in relevant cell
          types, and our method accurately predicts known drug-disease pairs
          while inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, we utilize a CRISPR
          screen to investigate lipid regulation, revealing functionally
          important players that lack associations but are prioritized within
          trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER.

          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that
          the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the
          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").


          Input paragraph: Genes act in concert with each other in specific
          contexts to perform their functions. Determining how these genes
          influence complex traits requires a mechanistic understanding of
          expression regulation across different conditions. It has been shown
          that this insight is critical for developing new therapies.
          Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped uncover the role of
          individual genes in disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern
          models of the architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene
          interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and progression.
          Here we introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
          gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a
          common latent representation for a joint analysis. This representation
          is based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
          the same conditions. We observe that diseases are significantly
          associated with gene modules expressed in relevant cell types, and our
          approach is accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and
          inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to
          analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important players
          lack associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
          PhenoPLIER.

          Background: Genetic studies have been crucial in understanding complex
          traits and disease etiology, but the importance of gene-gene
          interactions remains largely unexplored. Functional genomics,
          particularly transcriptome-wide association studies, has revealed
          individual genes' roles in various diseases; however, a mechanistic

          In the field of genetic studies and functional genomics, understanding
          how gene expression patterns contribute to complex traits remains a
          critical gap in our knowledge. This is particularly relevant for drug
          repurposing efforts, as identifying molecular mechanisms underlying

          repurposing strategies.

          follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to the
          reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients the
          reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
          research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands on
          the open question that the research answered. A successful context
          section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s contributions
          from the current state of the art by communicating what is missing in
          the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e.,
          the connection between the specific gap and the broader context that

          novel method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question.
          Then you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
          Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the question
          that was posed at the end of the context section. There is often a
          second part to the conclusion section that highlights how this
          conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e., "broader
          significance").

        - raw: >-
            You are a scientist with copy-editing skills who will help in
            improving the text of a manuscript with title '{{ title }}' and
            keywords '{{ keywords }}.' Revise the following abstract of this
            manuscript, so it has a clear sentence structure and follows a
            context-content-conclusion (C-C-C) scheme and fits in a single
            paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely necessary to
            follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the abstract must
            follow the following structure: 1) The context must communicate to
            the reader what gap the paper will fill. The first sentence orients
            the reader by introducing the broader field in which the particular
            research is situated. Then, this context is narrowed until it lands
            on the open question that the research answered. A successful
            context section sets the stage for distinguishing the paper’s
            contributions from the current state of the art by communicating
            what is missing in the literature (i.e., the specific gap) and why
            that matters (i.e., the connection between the specific gap and the
            broader context that the paper opened with); 2) The content ("Here
            we") first describes the novel method or approach that you used to
            fill the gap or question. Then you present the meat—your executive
            summary of the results; 3) Finally, the conclusion interprets the
            results to answer the question that was posed at the end of the
            context section. There is often a second part to the conclusion
            section that highlights how this conclusion moves the broader field
            forward (i.e., "broader significance").

              ---

              Genes collaborate with each other to perform their functions in
              specific contexts. To understand how these genes influence complex
              traits, a mechanistic understanding of expression regulation
              across different conditions is essential for developing novel
              therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have identified
              the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms. However,
              modern models suggest that gene-gene interactions play a crucial
              role in disease origin and progression.


              PhenoPLIER is a computational approach designed to map gene-trait
              associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
              latent representation for joint analysis. This representation is
              based on modules of genes with similar expression patterns across
              the same conditions, highlighting their importance in
              understanding diseases' etiology and drug mechanisms. We observe
              that diseases are significantly associated with gene modules
              expressed in relevant cell types and find our approach to be
              accurate in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
              mechanisms of action.


              Moreover, using a CRISPR screen for analyzing lipid regulation, we
              identify functionally important players lacking associations but
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In
              conclusion, integrating groups of co-expressed genes through the
              lens of gene modules provides context to genetic associations,
              enabling the discovery and validation of potential targets missed
              by single-gene strategies.


              PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting genetic
              associations and exploring disease etiology, providing valuable
              insights into drug repurposing and mechanisms of action.

              ---

              This manuscript aims to bridge the gap between genetic studies and
              functional genomics by utilizing gene co-expression patterns to
              elucidate disease etiology, drug mechanisms, and therapeutic
              targets. To achieve this, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel
              computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation for joint analysis. This method is based on modules
              of genes with similar expression patterns across the same
              conditions, thereby capturing gene-gene interactions in complex
              traits.


              We demonstrate the effectiveness of PhenoPLIER by accurately
              predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of
              action. Furthermore, using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid
              regulation, we find that functionally important players lack
              associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules by
              PhenoPLIER. In conclusion, PhenoPLIER provides a novel framework
              for interpreting genetic associations through the lens of gene
              modules, contextualizing these relationships and revealing
              potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. By integrating
              groups of co-expressed genes, this approach sheds light on complex
              traits and has broad implications in drug repurposing efforts.

              Genetic studies have advanced our understanding of complex traits,
              but a mechanistic understanding of gene expression regulation
              across different conditions is crucial for developing new
              therapies. Transcriptome-wide association studies have helped
              uncover the role of individual genes in disease mechanisms;

              and pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent

              associations.

              through the lens of gene modules, revealing potential targets
              missed by single-gene strategies and offering a novel framework
              for interpreting genetic data.

              The genetic basis of complex traits and diseases remains elusive
              due to the intricate interplay between genes in specific contexts.
              Understanding gene regulation is critical for developing new
              therapies, yet transcriptome-wide association studies alone cannot
              fully capture this complexity. Modern models predict that gene
              interactions play a crucial role in disease origin and
              progression.


              PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach, maps gene-trait
              associations and pharmacological perturbation data into a common
              latent representation for joint analysis. It identifies modules of
              co-expressed genes with similar expression patterns across the
              same conditions, revealing significant associations between
              diseases and these modules. This study demonstrates PhenoPLIER's
              accuracy in predicting known drug-disease pairs and inferring
              mechanisms of action. Furthermore, using CRISPR screening to
              analyze lipid regulation, we find that functionally important
              players are prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER
              despite lacking associations.


              In conclusion, PhenoPLIER contextualizes genetic associations
              through the lens of gene modules, revealing potential targets
              missed by single-gene strategies. This approach provides a novel
              framework for interpreting genetic associations and drug
              mechanisms, thus advancing our understanding of complex traits and
              diseases.

              disease-relevant mechanisms. However, modern models of the
              architecture of complex traits predict that gene-gene interactions
              play a crucial role in disease origin and progression. Here we
              introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that maps
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a common latent representation for a joint analysis. This
              representation is base on modules of genes with similar expression
              patterns across the same conditions. We observe that diseases are
              significantl associated with gene modules expressed in relevant
              cell types, and our approach is accurate in predicting known
              drug-disease pairs and inferring mechanisms of action. Furthermore
              using a CRISPR screen to analyze lipid regulation, we find that
              functionally important players lack associations but are
              prioritized in trait-associated modules by PhenoPLIER. In
              conclusion, by incorporating, groups of co-expressed genes,
              PhenoPLIER can contextualize genetic associations and reveal,
              potential targets missed by single-gene strategies. PhenoPLIER
              provides a novel framework for interpreting genetic associations
              through the lens of gene modules.

              In this study, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel computational
              method that facilitates the mapping of gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation for joint analysis. We emphasize the collaborative
              nature of genes in performing their functions; to understand how
              these genes influence complex traits requires a mechanistic
              understanding of expression regulation across different
              conditions. This insight is essential for developing new
              therapies, as transcriptome-wide association studies have
              uncovered the role of individual genes in disease-relevant
              mechanisms. However, modern models predict that gene-gene
              interactions play a critical role in disease origin and
              progression.


              PhenoPLIER's approach relies on modules of co-expressed genes with
              similar expression patterns across relevant cell types to
              associate diseases significantly with these functional units. Our
              method is accurate at predicting known drug-disease pairs, as well
              as inferring mechanisms of action. Further, using a CRISPR screen
              for lipid regulation analysis, we find that functionally important
              players in trait-associated modules lack associations but are
              prioritized by PhenoPLIER.


              In conclusion, incorporating groups of co-expressed genes helps
              contextualize genetic associations and reveal potential targets
              missed by single-gene strategies. By utilizing gene modules,
              PhenoPLIER offers a novel framework for interpreting complex
              traits and identifying therapeutic targets. This approach provides
              valuable insights into the disease etiology and drug mechanisms
              that could guide future research in functional genomics.

              ---

              We present PhenoPLIER, a cutting-edge computational framework that
              enables the mapping of gene-trait associations and pharmacological
              perturbation data into a unified latent representation for joint
              analysis. By understanding how genes collaborate to perform their
              functions in concert with each other under various conditions, we
              can more accurately predict complex traits. Recent
              transcriptome-wide association studies have demonstrated the
              critical role of individual genes in disease mechanisms; however,
              modern models suggest that gene-gene interactions play an
              essential part in diseases' origins and progression. 


              PhenoPLIER capitalizes on modules of co-expressed genes with
              similar patterns across specific conditions to project genetic
              associations and drug repurposing potential. Our approach has
              shown remarkable accuracy in predicting known drug-disease pairs,
              as well as identifying mechanisms of action for drugs targeting
              complex traits. Notably, we have also applied PhenoPLIER to a
              CRISPR screen focusing on lipid regulation, revealing functionally
              important players not associated with traits but prioritized by
              our framework within trait-associated modules. 


              In summary, PhenoPLIER's novel approach contextualizes genetic
              associations through gene modules and identifies potential targets
              missed by single-gene strategies. Our study highlights the power
              of this framework in interpreting complex biological systems and
              offers a promising avenue for drug repurposing efforts. By
              incorporating groups of co-expressed genes into our analysis, we
              can gain valuable insights into the etiology and underlying
              mechanisms of diseases.

              ---

              Background: Genetic studies have been crucial in understanding
              complex traits and disease etiology, but the importance of
              gene-gene interactions remains largely unexplored. Functional
              genomics, particularly transcriptome-wide association studies, has
              revealed individual genes' roles in various diseases; however, a
              mechanistic understanding of gene expression regulation across
              different conditions is necessary for developing new therapies.


              Methods: We introduce PhenoPLIER, a computational approach that
              maps gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data
              into a common latent representation for joint analysis. By
              identifying modules of genes with similar expression patterns
              across the same conditions, we discovered significant associations
              between diseases and these gene modules in relevant cell types.
              Our method accurately predicted known drug-disease pairs and
              inferred mechanisms of action.


              Results: We applied PhenoPLIER to analyze lipid regulation using a
              CRISPR screen and found that functionally important players lack
              associations but are prioritized in trait-associated modules,
              further supporting the utility of our approach.


              Conclusion: The application of PhenoPLIER highlights its potential
              for drug repurposing and therapeutic target identification by
              revealing gene-gene interactions and mechanisms underlying complex
              traits and diseases. Our work fills a gap in current literature,
              emphasizing the importance of integrating functional genomics with
              pharmacological perturbation data to understand disease etiology
              and develop effective therapies.

              traits requires a mechanistic approach to gene expression
              regulation across different conditions. Transcriptome-wide
              association studies have helped uncover the role of individual
              genes in disease mechanisms; however, modern models predict that
              gene-gene interactions play a crucial role in disease etiology and
              progression. 


              PhenoPLIER is a novel computational framework designed to map
              gene-trait associations into a common latent representation for
              joint analysis, based on modules of similar expression patterns
              across the same conditions. Our approach accurately predicts known
              drug-disease pairs and infers mechanisms of action from
              pharmacological perturbation data. Furthermore, using CRISPR
              screening in relevant cell types, we identify functionally
              important players lacking associations but prioritized by
              PhenoPLIER within trait-associated gene modules. This highlights
              the potential for repurposing existing drugs to target these
              disease pathways, providing new therapeutic opportunities and
              insights into complex traits associated with various diseases.

              ---

              In the field of genetic studies and functional genomics,
              understanding how gene expression patterns contribute to complex
              traits remains a critical gap in our knowledge. This is
              particularly relevant for drug repurposing efforts, as identifying
              molecular mechanisms underlying disease etiology can significantly
              impact therapeutic targets. The current literature primarily
              focuses on individual gene associations with specific conditions
              while neglecting the intricate interplay among genes and their
              co-expression patterns.


              To address this gap, we introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel
              computational approach that maps gene-trait associations and
              pharmacological perturbation data into a common latent
              representation for joint analysis. Our method is based on modules
              of genes exhibiting similar expression patterns across relevant
              conditions, providing insights into the underlying mechanisms
              driving disease etiology. By applying PhenoPLIER to existing
              datasets, we demonstrate its accuracy in predicting known
              drug-disease pairs, revealing novel molecular targets and
              elucidating therapeutic mechanisms.


              Furthermore, our study reveals that functionally important players
              identified through a CRISPR screen for lipid regulation are
              prioritized by phenotypic traits associated with disease but lack
              associations themselves. These findings highlight the potential of
              PhenoPLIER to identify novel drug candidates and illuminate
              previously unexplored aspects of complex trait etiology. In
              conclusion, this work advances our understanding of gene-gene
              interactions and their impact on complex diseases while offering
              promising avenues for drug repurposing strategies.

              in a single paragraph. Make changes only when they are absolutely
              necessary to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the
              abstract must follow the following structure: 1) The context must
              communicate to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The first
              sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
              which the particular research is situated. Then, this context is
              narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
              answered. A successful context section sets the stage for
              distinguishing the paper’s contributions from the current state of
              the art by communicating what is missing in the literature (i.e.,
              the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e., the connection
              between the specific gap and the broader context that the paper
              opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the novel
              method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question. Then
              you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)
              Finally, the conclusion interprets the results to answer the
              question that was posed at the end of the context section. There
              is often a second part to the conclusion section that highlights
              how this conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e.,
              "broader significance").

              ---

              Genes work together in specific contexts to perform their
              functions, and understanding how these genes contribute to complex
              traits requires a mechanistic analysis of expression regulation
              across various conditions. Transcriptome-wide association studies
              have contributed significantly to identifying the role of
              individual genes in disease mechanisms; however, modern models
              predict that gene-gene interactions play a critical role in
              disease etiology and progression. To address this challenge, we
              present PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach for mapping
              gene-trait associations and pharmacological perturbation data into
              a common latent representation suitable for joint analysis.


              PhenoPLIER is based on modules of genes with similar expression
              patterns across the same conditions, allowing us to observe
              significant associations between diseases and these gene modules
              in relevant cell types. Our method accurately predicts known
              drug-disease pairs and identifies mechanisms of action.
              Furthermore, we investigate lipid regulation using a CRISPR screen
              and find that functionally important players are prioritized by
              PhenoPLIER in trait-associated modules, providing insights into
              novel therapeutic targets for drug repurposing.


              In conclusion, the development of new therapies requires
              understanding gene interactions within complex traits; our
              approach offers valuable tools to dissect disease etiology and
              identify potential therapeutic targets through the analysis of
              transcriptomic data.

              ---

              Genes work together in concert to perform their functions, and
              understanding how these genes influence complex traits requires a
              mechanistic understanding of expression regulation across
              different conditions. Recent studies have shown that this insight
              is crucial for developing new therapies. Transcriptome-wide
              association studies have helped uncover the role of individual
              genes in disease mechanisms; however, modern models predict that
              gene-gene interactions play a significant role in disease etiology
              and progression.


              We introduce PhenoPLIER, a novel computational approach that maps
              gene-trait associations with pharmacological perturbation data
              into a common latent representation for joint analysis. This
              method is based on modules of genes exhibiting similar expression
              patterns across the same conditions, allowing us to project
              genetic associations through gene co-expression networks and
              highlight disease etiology as well as drug mechanisms.


              Our results indicate that diseases are significantly associated

              necessary to follow the C-C-C scheme. Under the C-C-C scheme, the
              abstract must follow the following structure: 1) The context must
              communicate to the reader what gap the paper will fill. The first
              sentence orients the reader by introducing the broader field in
              which the particular research is situated. Then, this context is
              narrowed until it lands on the open question that the research
              answered. A successful context section sets the stage for
              distinguishing the paper’s contributions from the current state of
              the art by communicating what is missing in the literature (i.e.,
              the specific gap) and why that matters (i.e., the connection
              between the specific gap and the broader context that the paper
              opened with); 2) The content ("Here we") first describes the novel
              method or approach that you used to fill the gap or question. Then
              you present the meat—your executive summary of the results; 3)

              question that was posed at the end of the context section. There
              is often a second part to the conclusion section that highlights
              how this conclusion moves the broader field forward (i.e.,
              "broader significance").
